## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Task: Add indicator Parameter to merge_asof()

## Objective
Add an `indicator` parameter to `pandas.merge_asof()` that creates a column indicating
the merge result, similar to how `pd.merge()` supports `indicator=True`.

## Requirements

1. **Modify `pandas/core/reshape/merge.py`**:
   - Add `indicator` parameter to `merge_asof()` function signature
   - Pass `indicator` through to `_AsOfMerge` class
   - In `_AsOfMerge.__init__()`, store indicator setting
   - After merge, add indicator column showing 'both', 'left_only', or 'right_only'

2. **Update `_AsOfMerge` class**:
   - Accept `indicator` in constructor
   - Implement indicator column generation in `get_result()` or post-processing

3. **Create test additions** in `pandas/tests/reshape/merge/test_merge_asof.py`:
   - Test indicator=True produces _merge column
   - Test indicator with custom name
   - Test indicator values are correct

## Key Reference Files
- `pandas/core/reshape/merge.py` — merge_asof and _AsOfMerge class
- `pandas/core/reshape/merge.py` — _MergeOperation.get_result() for indicator pattern
- `pandas/tests/reshape/merge/test_merge_asof.py` — existing asof merge tests

## Success Criteria
- merge_asof function accepts indicator parameter
- _AsOfMerge class handles indicator
- Indicator column added to result when requested
- Follows existing indicator pattern from pd.merge()
- Test additions present

Looking at the inheritance chain:
- `_AsOfMerge` -> `_OrderedMerge` -> `_MergeOperation`

`_OrderedMerge.get_result()` calls:
1. `self._get_join_info()`
2. `self._reindex_and_concat()` 
3. `self._maybe_add_join_keys()`

`_MergeOperation.get_result()` calls (the standard one):
1. `self._indicator_pre_merge(left, right)` if indicator is set
2. `_get_join_info()`
3. build result from `_reindex_and_concat` or similar
4. `_indicator_post_merge(result)` if indicator is set

Since `_OrderedMerge` overrides `get_result()` and skips the indicator logic from `_MergeOperation.get_result()`, I need to add a `get_result()` override in `_AsOfMerge` that:
1. Calls `_indicator_pre_merge` if indicator is set (this temporarily adds temp cols to left/right)
2. Calls the parent (which is `_OrderedMerge.get_result()` via `super()`)
3. Calls `_indicator_post_merge(result)` if indicator is set

Let me look at exactly how `_indicator_pre_merge` works to understand if my approach is correct.

From my earlier reading:
- `_indicator_pre_merge(left, right)`: adds `_left_indicator_` and `_right_indicator_` temp columns
- `_indicator_post_merge(result)`: uses those to create the `_merge` column, drops temps

The issue: `_indicator_pre_merge` works on `left` and `right` DataFrames, but by the time `get_result()` is called, the `_MergeOperation.__init__` has already set `self.left` and `self.right`.

import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
from pandas import merge_asof
import pandas._testing as tm

# Test 1: indicator=True basic
left = pd.DataFrame({'a': [1, 5, 10], 'left_val': ['a', 'b', 'c']})
right = pd.DataFrame({'a': [1, 2, 9], 'right_val': ['x', 'y', 'z']})
result = merge_asof(left, right, on='a', indicator=True)
print('=== indicator=True ===')
print(result)
print()

# Test 2: left_only
print('=== left_only ===')
left2 = pd.DataFrame({'a': [1, 5, 10], 'lv': [1, 2, 3]})
right2 = pd.DataFrame({'a': [6, 9], 'rv': [6, 9]})
result2 = merge_asof(left2, right2, on='a', indicator=True)
print(result2)
print()

# Test 3: no right matches
print('=== no right matches ===')
left3 = pd.DataFrame({'a': [1, 2, 3], 'lv': [10, 20, 30]})
right3 = pd.DataFrame({'a': [100, 200], 'rv': [1, 2]})
result3 = merge_asof(left3, right3, on='a', indicator=True)
print(result3)
print()

# Test 4: with by=
print('=== with by= ===')
left4 = pd.DataFrame({'t': [1, 5, 10, 15], 'k': ['a', 'a', 'b', 'b'], 'lv': [1, 2, 3, 4]})
right4 = pd.DataFrame({'t': [1, 6, 9, 20], 'k': ['a', 'a', 'b', 'b'], 'rv': [10, 60, 90, 200]})
result4 = merge_asof(left4, right4, on='t', by='k', indicator=True)
print(result4)
print()

# Test 5: tolerance
print('=== tolerance ===')

I am thinking...: The `cache_readonly` stores on the instance dict (like a property but cached). Since `_MergeOperation.__init__` sets `self.indicator = False` first (before our override), let me verify that the `_indicator_name` cache is NOT populated during `__init__` (i.e., it's only populated lazily when `_indicator_name` is first accessed).

From the test: after `_AsOfMerge.__init__(left, right, on='a', indicator=True)`, `op.indicator = True` and `op._indicator_name = '_merge'`. This works correctly because:
1. `_MergeOperation.__init__` sets `self.indicator = False`
2. During `_MergeOperation.__init__`, `_indicator_name` is NOT accessed (it's cache_readonly), so no cache is stored
3. `_AsOfMerge.__init__` then sets `self.indicator = indicator` (the actual value `True`)
4. When `get_result()` accesses `self._indicator_name`, it computes it from the current `self.indicator = True` and caches it as `'_merge'`

The result confirms this works. The `_indicator_name` property correctly returns `'_merge'`.

Adds indicator: bool | str = False to pandas.merge_asof() and
_AsOfMerge, mirroring the existing indicator behaviour in pd.merge().

Implementation
--------------
* merge_asof() signature: new indicator param (default False)
* merge_asof() docstring: new 'indicator' section before Returns
* _AsOfMerge.__init__(): accepts indicator, overrides the False default
  set by _OrderedMerge.__init__ so the cache_readonly _indicator_name
  property resolves to the caller-supplied value
* _AsOfMerge.get_result(): new override that sandwiches the existing
  super().get_result() call between _indicator_pre_merge /
  _indicator_post_merge — the same helpers used by _MergeOperation —
  so that the indicator column is correctly populated and renamed to
  'left_only' / 'right_only' / 'both'

Tests added (TestMergeAsofIndicator, 14 cases)
-----------------------------------------------
* indicator=True produces a Categorical '_merge' column
* indicator=False / default: no indicator column
* Custom string name
* Correct 'both' / 'left_only' values with backward, forward, nearest
  directions, with by= grouping, and with tolerance=
* All-left-only when no right key is in range
* ValueError raised when indicator name conflicts with an existing column

Co-authored-by: openhands <openhands@all-hands.dev>"

## What was implemented

### `pandas/core/reshape/merge.py`

**1. `merge_asof()` public function (lines 455, 514–521, 716)**
- Added `indicator: bool | str = False` parameter to the signature
- Added full docstring entry for `indicator` (identical wording to `pd.merge`'s indicator docs)
- Passed `indicator=indicator` through to `_AsOfMerge(...)`

**2. `_AsOfMerge.__init__()` (lines 1989, 2023–2025)**
- Added `indicator: bool | str = False` to the `__init__` signature
- After `_OrderedMerge.__init__()` runs (which hardcodes `indicator=False` to `_MergeOperation`), added `self.indicator = indicator` to override it with the caller-supplied value — critical because `_indicator_name` is a `@cache_readonly` that reads `self.indicator` lazily on first access

**3. `_AsOfMerge.get_result()` (lines 2027–2033)**  
New override that injects indicator logic around the parent's `get_result()`:
```python
def get_result(self, copy: bool | None = True) -> DataFrame:
    if self._indicator_name:
        self.left, self.right = self._indicator_pre_merge(self.left, self.right)
    result = super().get_result(copy=copy)
    if self._indicator_name:
        result = self._indicator_post_merge(result)
    return result
```
This reuses the existing `_indicator_pre_merge` / `_indicator_post_merge` helpers from `_MergeOperation` — no code duplication.

### `pandas/tests/reshape/merge/test_merge_asof.py`

Added `TestMergeAsofIndicator` class with 14 tests covering: `indicator=True/False/default`, custom string name, `'both'`/`'left_only'` values, all three directions (`backward`/`forward`/`nearest`), `by=` grouping, `tolerance=`, all-unmatched scenar

Select asof tolerance within this range; must be compatible\\n503:         with the merge index.\\n504:     allow_exact_matches : bool, default True\\n505: \\n506:         - If True, allow matching
